<div id="contentSub2"></div>

<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Culturally recognised union between people</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Marriage_(disambiguation)" title="Marriage (disambiguation)">Marriage (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Married" and "Matrimony" redirect here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Married_(disambiguation)" title="Married (disambiguation)">Married (disambiguation)</a> and <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Matrimony_(disambiguation)" title="Matrimony (disambiguation)">Matrimony (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:235px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gehrts_Armin_verabschiedet_sich_von_Thusnelda_1884.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2155" data-file-width="1517" decoding="async" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Gehrts_Armin_verabschiedet_sich_von_Thusnelda_1884.jpg/233px-Gehrts_Armin_verabschiedet_sich_von_Thusnelda_1884.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Gehrts_Armin_verabschiedet_sich_von_Thusnelda_1884.jpg/350px-Gehrts_Armin_verabschiedet_sich_von_Thusnelda_1884.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Gehrts_Armin_verabschiedet_sich_von_Thusnelda_1884.jpg/466px-Gehrts_Armin_verabschiedet_sich_von_Thusnelda_1884.jpg 2x" width="233"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gehrts_Armin_verabschiedet_sich_von_Thusnelda_1884.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The ancient <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a> married couple <a href="/wiki/Arminius" title="Arminius">Arminius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thusnelda" title="Thusnelda">Thusnelda</a> engaged in a romantic encounter. Created in 1884 by <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Gehrts" title="Johannes Gehrts">Johannes Gehrts</a>, the art piece depicts Arminius saying farewell to his beloved wife before he goes off into battle.</div></div></div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:An_Islamic_wedding_for_a_new_Bride_and_groom.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2100" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="308" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/An_Islamic_wedding_for_a_new_Bride_and_groom.jpg/220px-An_Islamic_wedding_for_a_new_Bride_and_groom.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/An_Islamic_wedding_for_a_new_Bride_and_groom.jpg/330px-An_Islamic_wedding_for_a_new_Bride_and_groom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/An_Islamic_wedding_for_a_new_Bride_and_groom.jpg/440px-An_Islamic_wedding_for_a_new_Bride_and_groom.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:An_Islamic_wedding_for_a_new_Bride_and_groom.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Islamic wedding</div></div></div>
<p><b>Marriage</b>, also called <b>matrimony</b> or <b>wedlock</b>, is a culturally and often legally recognized union between people called <a href="/wiki/Spouse" title="Spouse">spouses</a>. It establishes rights and obligations between them, as well as between them and their children, and between them and their <a href="/wiki/Affinity_(law)" title="Affinity (law)">in-laws</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> It is considered a <a href="/wiki/Cultural_universal" title="Cultural universal">cultural universal</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Couldn't find in the body. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> but the definition of marriage varies between cultures and religions, and over time. Typically, it is an <a href="/wiki/Institution" title="Institution">institution</a> in which interpersonal relationships, usually <a href="/wiki/Human_sexual_activity" title="Human sexual activity">sexual</a>, are acknowledged or sanctioned. In some cultures, marriage is recommended or considered to be <a href="/wiki/Premarital_sex" title="Premarital sex">compulsory before pursuing any sexual activity</a>. A marriage ceremony is called a <a href="/wiki/Wedding" title="Wedding">wedding</a>.
</p><p>Individuals may marry for several reasons, including legal, social, <a href="/wiki/Libido" title="Libido">libidinal</a>, emotional, financial, <a href="/wiki/Spirituality" title="Spirituality">spiritual</a>, and religious purposes. Whom they marry may be influenced by <a href="/wiki/Gender" title="Gender">gender</a>, <a href="/wiki/Incest_taboo" title="Incest taboo">socially determined rules of incest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alliance_theory" title="Alliance theory">prescriptive marriage rules</a>, parental choice, and individual desire. In some areas of the world, <a href="/wiki/Arranged_marriage" title="Arranged marriage">arranged marriage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Child_marriage" title="Child marriage">child marriage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">polygamy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Forced_marriage" title="Forced marriage">forced marriage</a> are practiced. In other areas, such practices are outlawed to preserve women's rights or children's rights (both female and male) or as a result of <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> In some parts of the world, marriage has historically restricted the rights of women, who are (or were) considered the property of the <a href="/wiki/Husband" title="Husband">husband</a>. Around the world, primarily in <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed</a> democracies, there has been a general trend towards ensuring <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women's rights">equal rights</a> for women within marriage (including abolishing <a href="/wiki/Coverture" title="Coverture">coverture</a>, liberalizing <a href="/wiki/Divorce" title="Divorce">divorce</a> laws, and reforming <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_rights" title="Reproductive rights">reproductive</a> and sexual rights) and legally recognizing the marriages of <a href="/wiki/Interfaith_marriage" title="Interfaith marriage">interfaith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interracial_marriage" title="Interracial marriage">interracial</a>/<a href="/wiki/Interethnic_marriage" title="Interethnic marriage">interethnic</a>/<a href="/wiki/Inter-caste_marriage" title="Inter-caste marriage">inter-caste</a> and <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex</a> couples. Controversies continue regarding the legal status of married women, leniency towards violence within marriage, customs such as <a href="/wiki/Dowry" title="Dowry">dowry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bride_price" title="Bride price">bride price</a>, forced marriage, <a href="/wiki/Marriageable_age" title="Marriageable age">marriageable age</a>, and criminalization of <a href="/wiki/Premarital_sex" title="Premarital sex">premarital</a> and <a href="/wiki/Extramarital_sex" title="Extramarital sex">extramarital sex</a>. Female age at marriage has proven to be a strong indicator for female <a href="/wiki/Autonomy" title="Autonomy">autonomy</a> and is continuously used by <a href="/wiki/Economic_history" title="Economic history">economic history</a> research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>Marriage can be recognized by a <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Organization" title="Organization">organization</a>, a religious authority, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tribal_group" title="Tribal group">tribal group</a>, a local <a href="/wiki/Community" title="Community">community</a>, or peers. It is often viewed as a <a href="/wiki/Contract" title="Contract">contract</a>. A religious marriage is performed by a religious institution to recognize and create the rights and obligations intrinsic to matrimony in that religion. Religious marriage is known variously as <a href="/wiki/Sacrament" title="Sacrament">sacramental marriage</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholicism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nikah" title="Nikah">nikah</a> in <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nissuin" title="Nissuin">nissuin</a> in <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, and various other names in other faith traditions, each with their own constraints as to what constitutes, and who can enter into, a valid religious marriage.
</p>
